GM purchased a controlling interest in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saab_Automobile" title="Saab Automobile">Saab</a> in 1990, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isuzu" title="Isuzu">Isuzu</a> in 1998 and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daewoo_Motors" title="Daewoo Motors">Daewoo Motors</a> in 2001, and invested in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subaru" title="Subaru">Subaru</a> in 1999 and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> in 2000, and also purchased the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a> name from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AM_General" title="AM General">AM General</a> in 1998.

--- Chunk 925 ---
Ford purchased a 33.4% controlling-interest in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in 1996 and acquired <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> in 1999 followed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> in May 2000.

--- Chunk 926 ---
GM and Ford also established joint ventures with Chinese auto companies during this period.

--- Chunk 927 ---
GM's joint ventures are with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shanghai_GM" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai GM">Shanghai GM</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAIC-GM-Wuling_Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile">SAIC-GM-Wuling Automobile</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FAW_Group" title="FAW Group">FAW-GM Light Duty Commercial Vehicle Co Ltd.</a> Ford's joint ventures are with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Changan_Ford_Mazda" title="Changan Ford Mazda">Chang'an Ford</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiangling_Motors" title="Jiangling Motors">Jiangling Ford</a>.

--- Chunk 928 ---
While the American automakers were investing in or buying foreign competitors, the foreign automakers continued to establish more production facilities in the United States.

--- Chunk 929 ---
In the 1990s, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daimler-Benz" class="mw-redirect" title="Daimler-Benz">Daimler-Benz</a> opened <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">SUV</a> factories in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spartanburg_County,_South_Carolina" title="Spartanburg County, South Carolina">Spartanburg County, South Carolina</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuscaloosa_County,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa County, Alabama">Tuscaloosa County, Alabama</a>, respectively.

--- Chunk 930 ---
In the 2000s, assembly plants were opened by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lincoln,_Alabama" title="Lincoln, Alabama">Lincoln, Alabama</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> in Canton, Mississippi, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montgomery,_Alabama" title="Montgomery, Alabama">Montgomery, Alabama</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kia_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Kia Motors">Kia</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Point,_Georgia" title="West Point, Georgia">West Point, Georgia</a>.

--- Chunk 931 ---
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> opened an engine plant in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville, Alabama</a>, in 2003, along with a truck assembly plant in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, and is building an assembly plant in Blue Springs, Mississippi.

--- Chunk 932 ---
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> has announced a new plant for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chattanooga,_Tennessee" title="Chattanooga, Tennessee">Chattanooga, Tennessee</a>.

--- Chunk 933 ---
Several of the Japanese auto manufacturers expanded or opened additional plants during this period.

--- Chunk 934 ---
For example, while new, the Alabama Daimler-Benz and Honda plants have expanded several times since their original construction.

--- Chunk 935 ---
The opening of Daimler-Benz plant in the 1990s had a cascade effect.

--- Chunk 936 ---
It created a hub of new sub-assembly suppliers in the Alabama area.

--- Chunk 937 ---
This hub of sub-assemblies suppliers helped in attracting several new assembly plants into Alabama plus new plants in nearby Mississippi, Georgia and Tennessee.

--- Chunk 938 ---
In 1998, Chrysler and the German automaker <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daimler-Benz" class="mw-redirect" title="Daimler-Benz">Daimler-Benz</a> entered into a "merger of equals" although in reality it turned out be an acquisition by Daimler-Benz.

--- Chunk 939 ---
Thus the Big Three American-owned automakers turned into the Big Two automakers.

--- Chunk 940 ---
However, a culture clash emerged between the two divisions, and there was an exodus of engineering and manufacturing management from the Chrysler division.

--- Chunk 941 ---
The Chrysler division struggled financially, with only a brief recovery when the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysler_300" title="Chrysler 300">Chrysler 300</a> was introduced.

--- Chunk 942 ---
In 2007, Daimler-Benz sold the company to a private equity firm, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerberus_Capital_Management" title="Cerberus Capital Management">Cerberus Capital Management</a>, thus again making it American-owned.

--- Chunk 943 ---
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">

--- Chunk 944 ---
<span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2000s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span>

--- Chunk 945 ---
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">

--- Chunk 946 ---
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Automobile_assembly_plants_in_the_USA_in_2004.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Automobile_assembly_plants_in_the_USA_in_2004.png/250px-Automobile_assembly_plants_in_the_USA_in_2004.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Automobile_assembly_plants_in_the_USA_in_2004.png/500px-Automobile_assembly_plants_in_the_USA_in_2004.png 1.5x" data-file-width="950" data-file-height="576" /></a>

--- Chunk 947 ---
Automobile assembly plants in the United States in 2004

--- Chunk 948 ---
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" />

--- Chunk 949 ---
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

--- Chunk 950 ---
See also: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_the_2008%E2%80%9310_automotive_industry_crisis_on_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Effects of the 2008–10 automotive industry crisis on the United States">Effects of the 2008–10 automotive industry crisis on the United States</a>

--- Chunk 951 ---
The 2000s began with a recession in early 2001 and the effects of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, significantly affecting auto industry sales and profitability.

--- Chunk 952 ---
The stock market decline affected the pension fund levels of the automakers, requiring significant contributions to the funds by the automakers (with GM financing these contributions by raising debt).

--- Chunk 953 ---
In 2001, Chrysler discontinued their <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Plymouth</a> brand, and in 2004 GM ended their <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oldsmobile" title="Oldsmobile">Oldsmobile</a> division.

--- Chunk 954 ---
In 2005, oil prices began rising and peaked in 2008.

--- Chunk 955 ---
With the American automakers heavily dependent upon the gas-guzzling light truck sales for their profits, their sales fell sharply.

--- Chunk 956 ---
Additionally, the finance subsidiaries of the Big Three became of increasing importance to their overall profitability (and their eventual downfall).

--- Chunk 957 ---
GMAC (now <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ally_Financial" title="Ally Financial">Ally Financial</a>), began making home mortgage loans, especially <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subprime" class="mw-redirect" title="Subprime">subprime</a> loans.

--- Chunk 958 ---
With the subsequent collapse of the sub-prime mortgage industry, GM suffered heavy losses.

--- Chunk 959 ---
The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_crisis_of_2008%E2%80%9310" class="mw-redirect" title="Automotive industry crisis of 2008–10">Automotive industry crisis of 2008–10</a> happened when the Big Three were in weak financial condition and the beginning of an economic recession, and the financial crisis resulted in the automakers looking to the federal government for help.

--- Chunk 960 ---
Ford was in the best position, as under new CEO <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> they had fortuitously raised $23 billion in cash in 2006 by mortgaging most of their assets.

--- Chunk 961 ---
Chrysler, purchased in 2007 by a private equity firm, had weak financial backing, was the most heavily dependent on light truck sales, and had few new products in their pipeline.

--- Chunk 962 ---
General Motors was highly leveraged, also heavily dependent on light truck sales, and burdened by high health care costs.

--- Chunk 963 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 964 ---
The CEOs of the Big Three requested government aid in November 2008, but sentiment in Congress was against the automakers, especially after it was revealed that they had flown to Washington, D.

--- Chunk 965 ---
C., on their private corporate jets.

--- Chunk 966 ---
In December 2008, President Bush gave $17.4 billion to GM and Chrysler from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a> as temporary relief for their cash flow problems.

--- Chunk 967 ---
Several months later, President Obama formed the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_Task_Force_on_the_Auto_Industry" title="Presidential Task Force on the Auto Industry">Presidential Task Force on the Auto Industry</a> to decide how to handle GM and Chrysler.

--- Chunk 968 ---
Chrysler received a total of $12.5 billion in TARP funds and entered Chapter 11 bankruptcy in April 2009.

--- Chunk 969 ---
Automaker <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat</a> was given management control and a 20% ownership stake (adjusted to 35% under certain conditions), the U.

--- Chunk 970 ---
S.  and Canadian governments were given a 10% holding, and the remaining ownership was given to a Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association (VEBA), which was a trust fund established to administer employee health care benefits.

--- Chunk 971 ---
The Automotive Task Force requested that GM CEO <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_Wagoner" title="Rick Wagoner">Rick Wagoner</a> resign, and he was replaced by another long-time GM executive, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_Henderson" title="Frederick Henderson">Frederick Henderson</a>.

--- Chunk 972 ---
GM received a total of $49.5 billion in TARP funds and entered Chapter 11 bankruptcy in June 2009.

--- Chunk 973 ---
S.  and Canadian governments received a 72.5% ownership stake, a VEBA received 17.5%, and the unsecured creditors received 10%.

--- Chunk 974 ---
As part of the bailout GM and Chrysler closed numerous production plants and eliminated hundreds of dealerships and thousands of jobs.

--- Chunk 975 ---
They also required a number of major labor union concessions.

--- Chunk 976 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-:0_62-0" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-:0-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 977 ---
GM sold off the Saab division and eliminated the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontiac_(automobile)" title="Pontiac (automobile)">Pontiac</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturn_Corporation" title="Saturn Corporation">Saturn Corporation</a> brands.

--- Chunk 978 ---
In addition to the $62 billion that the automakers received from TARP, their financing arms, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ally_Financial" title="Ally Financial">Ally Financial</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TD_Auto_Finance" title="TD Auto Finance">TD Auto Finance</a> received an additional $17.8 billion.

--- Chunk 979 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-:0_62-1" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-:0-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition to the funding from the United States government, the Canadian government provided $10.8 billion to GM and $2.9 billion to Chrysler as incentives to maintain production facilities in Canada.

--- Chunk 980 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 981 ---
Ford did not request any government assistance, but as part of their downsizing decided in 2009 to sell <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a>, which was acquired by Chinese <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geely" title="Geely">Geely</a> in the summer of 2010, and phased out their <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> division in 2011.  (Ford had previously sold <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> in 2007, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar Cars</a> in early-June 2008 and its controlling-interest in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in November 2008).

--- Chunk 982 ---
Under the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_Technology_Vehicles_Manufacturing_Loan_Program" title="Advanced Technology Vehicles Manufacturing Loan Program">Advanced Technology Vehicles Manufacturing Loan Program</a> Ford borrowed $5.9 billion to help their vehicles meet higher mileage requirements.

--- Chunk 983 ---
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">

--- Chunk 984 ---
<span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2010s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span>

--- Chunk 985 ---
Ford went through 2012 having recovered to the point of having 80,000 total U.

--- Chunk 986 ---
S.  employees, supplying their 3,300 dealerships.

--- Chunk 987 ---
In comparison, Chrysler had 71,100 U.

--- Chunk 988 ---
S.  employees supplying their 2,328 dealerships during that year.

--- Chunk 989 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-money-go_14-1" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-money-go-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 990 ---
Data for the beginning of 2014 put the four companies of GM, Ford, Toyota, and Chrysler, in that order, at the top as having the most U.

--- Chunk 991 ---
In terms of specific types of vehicles, the new decade has meant Chrysler having an emphasis on its Ram trucks and the Jeep Cherokee SUV, both of which had "hefty sales" for 2014 according to a news report.

--- Chunk 992 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 993 ---
In 2014, Fiat, now named <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat Chrysler">Fiat Chrysler</a>, established full control of ownership of Chrysler and its divisions (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodge" title="Dodge">Dodge</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeep" title="Jeep">Jeep</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ram_Trucks" title="Ram Trucks">Ram Trucks</a>)

--- Chunk 994 ---
In 2017, it is reported that auto makers spent more on incentives, US$3,830 per vehicle sold, than labour, which is estimated to be less than US$2,500 per vehicle.

--- Chunk 995 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 996 ---
In 2017, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> sold its <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors_Europe" title="General Motors Europe">European</a> brands, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a>, to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groupe_PSA" class="mw-redirect" title="Groupe PSA">Groupe PSA</a> due to low profits.

--- Chunk 997 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also announced the closure of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> plant in Australia, making Holden an import brand.

--- Chunk 998 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 999 ---
In 2019, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> closed 5 plants.

--- Chunk 1000 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also pulled out of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>.

--- Chunk 1001 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1002 ---
Near the end of the decade, it became clear that the market now has a preference for crossover SUVs over passenger cars.

--- Chunk 1003 ---
In 2016, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat Chrysler">Fiat Chrysler</a> announced that it would be discontinuing the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodge_Dart_(PF)" title="Dodge Dart (PF)">Dodge Dart</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chrysler_200" title="Chrysler 200">Chrysler 200</a> sedans.

--- Chunk 1004 ---
CEO <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergio_Marchionne" title="Sergio Marchionne">Sergio Marchionne</a> said that, even though they were good cars, they were the least financially rewarding investments the company has made recently.

--- Chunk 1005 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1006 ---
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a>, in 2018, announced that it will be discontinuing all of its passenger cars save for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Mustang" title="Ford Mustang">Ford Mustang</a>, and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Ford Focus</a> would come back as a crossover-hatchback vehicle known as the Ford Focus Active.

--- Chunk 1007 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ford later cancelled plans of selling the Ford Focus Active in the United States and Canada as a result of the Trump Administration imposing tariffs on all Chinese built vehicles due to China's human rights violations, leading to a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China-United_States_Trade_War" class="mw-redirect" title="China-United States Trade War">China-United States Trade War</a> as the Ford Focus Active for the US and Canadian markets would be imported from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Changan_Ford" title="Changan Ford">Changan Ford</a> factory in Harbin, Heilongjiang Province, China.

--- Chunk 1008 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> followed by saying it would not follow Ford, however, backtracked on that and announced that it would be discontinuing most of its passenger cars by 2022.

--- Chunk 1009 ---
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2">

--- Chunk 1010 ---
<span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2020s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span>

--- Chunk 1011 ---
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" />

--- Chunk 1012 ---
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">

--- Chunk 1013 ---
See also: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_automobile_manufacturers_of_the_United_States" title="List of automobile manufacturers of the United States">List of automobile manufacturers of the United States</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_American_truck_manufacturers" title="List of American truck manufacturers">List_of_American_truck_manufacturers</a>

--- Chunk 1014 ---
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb">

--- Chunk 1015 ---
<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2025_Growth_in_truck_size.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2025_Growth_in_truck_size.svg/250px-2025_Growth_in_truck_size.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2025_Growth_in_truck_size.svg/500px-2025_Growth_in_truck_size.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="675" /></a>

--- Chunk 1016 ---
S., pickup trucks have grown in size and function, from workhorses to family vehicles with many technological features.

--- Chunk 1017 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-Axios_20230123_73-0" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-Axios_20230123-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the 2010s, small pickups had nearly vanished and in the 2020s full-size trucks made up a majority of U.

--- Chunk 1018 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-Axios_20230123_73-1" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-Axios_20230123-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Safety advocates are concerned with larger trucks' mass and driver blind spots.

--- Chunk 1019 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-Axios_20230123_73-2" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-Axios_20230123-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1020 ---
In 2020, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> announced the end of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a> and that it planned to leave <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> by 2021.

--- Chunk 1021 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> General Motors also announced its exit from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thai</a> market and plans to sell their <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rayong" title="Rayong">Rayong</a> plant.

--- Chunk 1022 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
In August 2021, Ford announced that it would be shutting down its India production as it was not able to have sufficient demand to justify running 2 plants.

--- Chunk 1023 ---
In January 2021, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiat Chrysler">Fiat Chrysler</a> (FCA) merged with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groupe_PSA" class="mw-redirect" title="Groupe PSA">Groupe PSA</a> hence making FCA's North American operations (including Dodge, Chrysler, Jeep and Ram) part of a brand new parent entity named <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stellantis" title="Stellantis">Stellantis</a>, which is headquartered in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="The Netherlands">The Netherlands</a>.

--- Chunk 1024 ---
On January 28, 2021, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> announced that it will become 100% all-electric by 2035 in order to become compliant with the Biden Administration's tougher automotive emission standards and electric vehicle goals due to worsening climate change and air pollution.

--- Chunk 1025 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1026 ---
By 2021, the only non-SUV, truck, or van that Ford produced was the Mustang pony car, while GM only produced the Malibu midsized sedan, the Camaro pony car and the luxury Cadillac <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cadillac_CT4" title="Cadillac CT4">CT4</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cadillac_CT5" title="Cadillac CT5">CT5</a>

--- Chunk 1027 ---
The late 2010s and early 2020s also saw the rise of electric-only brand <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tesla_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla</a>, which became the most valuable automaker in the world by market capitalization in January 2020, and produced over half a million cars in 2020.

--- Chunk 1028 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1029 ---
The decade has also seen the rise of electric cars in general, and in 2020 roughly 2 percent of all new cars sold were fully electric.

--- Chunk 1030 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1031 ---
According to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_Investment_and_Jobs_Act" title="Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act">Infrastructure Investment and Jobs Act</a>, by 2026, all new passenger vehicles sold must be equipped with systems that do not allow the vehicle to turn on if blood alcohol content level is above the amount permissible by law.

--- Chunk 1032 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The legislation is not clear what form this detection would take, the wording states that the monitoring would be "passive" which will possibly require the use of cameras in order to properly track and monitor driver behavior.

--- Chunk 1033 ---
Proponents of this change state that it will reduce drunk driving deaths on the road while opponents argue that it is a violation of privacy of drivers and that drivers could experience technical difficulties while on the road.

--- Chunk 1034 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1035 ---
In December 2021, the Biden administration imposed Executive Order 14057, which is a nationwide federal government mandate that will ban new fossil fuel vehicles from all 50 US States, Washington, D.

--- Chunk 1036 ---
C., and all US Territories by 2035 to push the transition to electric vehicles.

--- Chunk 1037 ---
The order will ban new car sales of fossil-fuel-powered government-owned vehicles by 2027, new fossil-fuel-powered buses by 2030, and both new fossil-fuel-powered privately owned vehicles and new fossil-fuel-powered commercial-owned vehicles by 2035.

--- Chunk 1038 ---
The US Environmental Protection Agency also unveiled stringent automotive emissions and fuel economy requirements for internal combustion engine-powered vehicles that will become mandatory on all new US-market ICE-powered vehicles starting for the 2023 model year.

--- Chunk 1039 ---
The standards will also get tougher and more stringent for the 2026, 2029, and 2032 model years.

--- Chunk 1040 ---
The new regulations will also require at least 20% of all-new vehicles sold in the United States to be 100% all-electric vehicles by 2026, followed by requiring at least 60% of all-new vehicles sold in the United States to be 100% all-electric vehicles by 2030, and finally followed by requiring 100% of all-new vehicles sold in the United States to be 100% all-electric vehicles by 2035.

--- Chunk 1041 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1042 ---
On April 12, 2023, the US Environmental Protection Agency Administrator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_S._Regan" title="Michael S. Regan">Michael Regan</a> proposed tougher automotive emissions standards wherein that 67 percent of all new light-duty highway vehicles sold nationwide must have no tailpipe greenhouse gas emissions by 2032 in order to reduce the probability of severe climate change and its consequences.

--- Chunk 1043 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1044 ---
In 2024, Volkswagen announced they would make a joint venture with electric car maker Rivian.

--- Chunk 1045 ---
Rivian is a competitor of Tesla.

--- Chunk 1046 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1047 ---
In 2024, plants from the United States produced 10.4 million vehicles, half of them were European or Asian brands, including Toyota, Honda, BMW and Mercedes.

--- Chunk 1048 ---
Some of those vehicles are exported to Canada and Mexico.

--- Chunk 1049 ---
In 2014, 4 million finished cars were produced; this number declined to 1.7 million finished cars in 2024.

--- Chunk 1050 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1051 ---
In 2025, some taxes are considered.

--- Chunk 1052 ---
Half of all vehicles sold in the United States are imported and 60 percent of parts of vehicles assembled in the United States.

--- Chunk 1053 ---
Those taxes would make auto companies and suppliers to set up shop in the United States.

--- Chunk 1054 ---
<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States.html#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>

--- Chunk 1055 ---
